  ├──────────────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A₀ (hw-installed)│ ~100-300ms  │ Taste receptor → brainstem →     │
  │                  │             │ opioid. Pre-compiled binary eval.│
  ├──────────────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A₁ (basic comp.) │ ~200ms-1s   │ Sensory → compiled chunks →     │
  │                  │             │ simple matching → opioid.        │
  ├──────────────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A₂ (complex comp)│ ~500ms-2s   │ Multi-chunk evaluation.         │
  │                  │             │ Context-dependent matching.       │
  ├──────────────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A₃ (deep comp.)  │ ~1-5s       │ Abstract schema fit. ACC         │
  │                  │             │ coherence → opioid pipeline.     │
  └──────────────────┴─────────────┴──────────────────────────────────┘

  ⚠️ Timing ranges = ESTIMATES from processing depth, not measured.
  But GRADIENT direction = strong framework prediction.

  ⭐ KEY INSIGHT: "First feel" of any experience = B or A₀.
  → A₁-A₃ layers arrive LATER with increasing delay.
  → Experience BUILDS over time as layers stack.
  → Ăn chocolate: vị ngọt (A₀ ~100ms) → "ngon" (A₁ ~500ms)
    → "ngon như lần ở Paris" (A₃ compare, ~2-5s)
  → Each layer ADDS to subjective richness.

  Liên kết R18: B onset nhanh VÌ bypass VTA → posterior insula directly.
  A cần VTA delta detect → PFC → evaluation → opioid = pipeline DÀI hơn.
  Liên kết R19: A₀ and B both hardware → SIMILAR onset (~100ms range).
  A₃ purely cortical → slowest onset but highest preview fidelity (R17).


  ❷ DECAY/AFTERGLOW = f(MECHANISM TYPE):

  R20 finding: A habituates via VTA (central, uniform).
  B habituates via receptor adaptation (peripheral, modality-specific).
  → FUNDAMENTALLY different decay curves:

  TYPE B DECAY — modality-specific:
    CT dynamic touch: ██████████████████████████████░░░
      (very slow — CT DESIGNED for sustained contact, 🟢 Löken 2009)
    Temperature:      ████████░░░░
      (fast — thermal physics, ~5-10 min)
    Exercise eCB:     ██████████████████████░░░░
      (slow — metabolic half-life)
    → NO "B decay rate" — each modality has own curve.

  TYPE A DECAY — via VTA + consolidation:
    A₀ sweet:    ████████████░░░░
      (moderate — brainstem, simple)
    A₁ food:     ██████████░░░░░
      (moderate — VTA habituates across session)
    A₂ music:    ████████████████░░░░░
      (longer — pattern complexity delays VTA habituation)
    A₃ insight:  ████▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓░░░░░░░░
      (burst + LONG afterglow — see ❸ below)

  → Higher A complexity = LONGER afterglow.
  → B decay = peripheral physics. A decay = central VTA + consolidation.


  ❸ WHY A₃ AFTERGLOW IS EXCEPTIONALLY LONG:

  Einstein: "DAYS of ecstasy" after E=mc².
  Hamilton: could not stop for hours, carved on bridge.
  Wiles: came back to desk repeatedly for 20 minutes.

  Framework explains: A₃ afterglow = 4 OVERLAPPING temporal curves,
  NOT single curve stretched:

    CURVE 1 — OPIOID CONSOLIDATION GLOW:
      Gap fill → opioid. But chunks STILL consolidating
      (Hebbian LTP, synaptic reorganization, late LTP).
      Each micro-consolidation step = mini-opioid pulse.
      Duration: hours → days.
      🟢 Consolidation = established (McGaugh 2000, synaptic → systems)

    CURVE 2 — RELIEF COMPOUND (cortisol drop gradient):
      Years of pending (Chunk-Gap) → cortisol baseline shifted high.
      Gap fill → cortisol DROP. But cortisol has INERTIA
      (BFM §3.3⑥: "Post-project blues" = cortisol drop takes days/weeks).
      Relief signal overlaps with opioid → COMPOUND.
      Duration: days → weeks (proportional to pending duration).

    CURVE 3 — BACKGROUND PROCESSING CASCADE:
      Insight creates new chunks → new chunks fire →
      network reorganizes → generates RELATED micro-insights.
      Each micro-insight = mini gap-fill → mini opioid.
      Einstein: E=mc² → implications unfold over days.
      "À, nó CŨNG có nghĩa..." = secondary discoveries.
      Duration: hours → days (until network stabilizes).
      🟢 Spreading activation (Collins & Loftus 1975)
      🟢 Sleep-dependent consolidation (Walker 2017)

    CURVE 4 — VERIFICATION LOOP (R4 finding):
      Coherence CAN be wrong → verification drive.
      Each recheck → "vẫn đúng" → ANOTHER opioid pulse.
      Wiles: 20 minutes recheck. Einstein: continuous verification.
      Duration: minutes → hours (until compiled as "confirmed").

    4 CURVES OVERLAPPING:
      t=0:      ████ opioid burst (curve 1)
      t=1min:   ████▓▓▓ + relief starting (curve 2) + recheck (curve 4)
      t=1h:     ▓▓▓▓▓▓ consolidation + relief + background (curves 1+2+3)
      t=6h:     ▓▓▓▓ consolidation + relief (curves 1+2) + sleep processing
      t=next day: ▓▓▓ relief gradient + "new implications!" (curves 2+3)
      t=2-3 days: ░░░ relief fading + occasional insight (curves 2+3)

    → A₃ afterglow = 4 mechanisms with DIFFERENT timescales OVERLAPPING.
    → NOT 1 signal "lasting days" — 4 signals taking turns sustaining.
    → A₀ afterglow SHORT because: minimal consolidation, no relief,
      no background cascade, no verification.
    → A₃ afterglow LONG because: ALL 4 mechanisms active.


  ❹ TEMPORAL STACK MODEL:

  Any experience at any moment = SUM of overlapping temporal profiles.
  "Richness" = number of active temporal layers + overlap quality.

  VÍ DỤ: Ăn cùng bạn bè (compound experience):

    Time→   0ms    200ms   500ms   1s     5s    30s   5min   1h
            ├──────┼───────┼──────┼──────┼─────┼─────┼──────┤
    B(touch): ░░░░░  (hand on arm — background, very slow decay)
    A₀(taste):      ████████████████████████░░░░
    A₁(food):                ████████████████████████░░░░░░░
    A₂(eval):                        ███████████████████░░░░░░
    ③Social:                                ████████████████████████████░░░░
    ④Relief:                                     ██████████████████████████░░░░░░░
    ⑤Preview:                                                            ▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓░░

    Total:   ░      ██      ████    █████ █████ █████  ███   ▓▓
             barely sweet   compound peak  rich  fading glow  memory

  → Compound experiences BUILD over time: nhiều layers arrive
    ở thời điểm khác nhau → subjective richness INCREASES.
  → Rush experiences (drugs, gambling) feel "shallow":
    1-2 layers only, peak nhanh, decay nhanh.
  → Deep compound experiences (social + sensory + coherence)
    feel "rich": nhiều layers, build dần, decay chậm.

  DURATION FORMULA (qualitative):
    Duration_total = f(source_type × A/B_type × compound_layers × pending)
    
    → Type B vs A: B = stimulus-bound, A = outlasts stimulus
    → A₀ vs A₃: A₃ >> A₀ (more cortical → more consolidation)
    → More pending (P1) → longer relief gradient → longer
    → More compound layers → wider temporal envelope
    → Background processing → extends A₃ specifically


  🔴 TESTABLE PREDICTIONS:

  P-R5a: B onset PRECEDES A onset for compound A+B stimulus
    → Posterior insula activates BEFORE NAcc/VTA
    → Testable: high-temporal-resolution fMRI (social touch)
    → Expected: ~50-100ms latency difference

  P-R5b: A₃ afterglow duration > A₁ afterglow duration
    → Expert insight glow lasts LONGER than simple pattern match
    → Testable: mood tracking after different complexity insights
    → Expected: A₃ hours-days, A₁ minutes-hours

  P-R5c: Compound experiences have WIDER temporal envelope
    → Duration_compound > max(Duration_component_i)
    → Not just sum — overlapping curves extend total
    → Testable: mood duration tracking for single vs compound experiences

  P-R5d: "Second wave" phenomenon for A₃ reward
    → A₃ reward can have delayed secondary peaks (hours later)
    → Background processing → related insights → opioid pulse
    → Testable: experience sampling method post-insight
    → "Oh, it ALSO means..." = delayed micro-insight = second wave


  CROSS-REFERENCES:
    → §2.3 Temporal Profile sketch → FORMALIZED here
    → §3.10 A₀→A₃ gradient → onset latency follows same gradient
    → §3.11 R20 B habituation → decay mechanism type determines curves
    → §3.12 R17 preview fidelity → A₃ highest fidelity + longest glow
    → §3.13 R18 insula gradient → B → posterior (fast), A → anterior (slower)
    → §7.3 R4 motor urgency → verification loop = afterglow curve 4
    → §3.15 R7 compound model → temporal overlap is 4th variable
    → BFM §3.3⑥ → cortisol inertia = mechanism for curve 2
    → Novelty.md §1 → VTA habituation = A-specific decay mechanism
    → 🟢 McGaugh 2000 — memory consolidation timescales
    → 🟢 Walker 2017 — sleep-dependent consolidation
    → 🟢 Collins & Loftus 1975 — spreading activation
    → 🟢 Löken 2009 — CT designed for sustained (slow adaptation)
```

### §3.15 — Compound Interaction Model (v0.7 new: R7 drill)

```
⭐⭐ R7 DRILL — COMPOUND PROFILES: INTERACTION MODEL

  QUESTION: Edge cases (§3.7) show compound = norm, not exception.
  BFM §4 has additive model: Signal_total = Σ (dynamics_i × intensity_i × network_size_i).
  But compound feels qualitatively DIFFERENT, not just STRONGER.
  Is interaction additive, multiplicative, or synergistic?

  ANSWER: NONE of the above exclusively.
  Interaction type DEPENDS ON 3 variables:
  substrate overlap, A gate direction, relief presence.
  → CONDITIONAL INTERACTION MODEL.


  ❶ WITHIN-TYPE INTERACTION (same substrate):

  A + A (same opioid pathway):
    → Food + Music: BOTH use μ-opioid hotspot (NAcc shell, VP)
    → Hotspot has finite capacity (~1mm³ vùng)
      🟢 Peciña & Berridge 2005: hotspot SMALL, specific
    → 2 signals converge → same receptors → CEILING EFFECT
    → Signal_total < Signal_A1 + Signal_A2
    → = SUBADDITIVE — diminishing returns

    Observable: Ăn ngon + nghe nhạc ĐỒNG THỜI → better than either alone
    BUT NOT double. One partially masks other.
    
    Evolutionary logic: if A+A purely additive → multiple A signals
    could overwhelm system → dopaminergic overload → loss of control.
    Ceiling = SAFETY MECHANISM.

    Within A level matters:
      A₁ + A₁ (food + music): MOST subadditive (both sensory opioid)
      A₁ + A₃ (food + insight): LESS subadditive (different pathways converging)
      A₃ + A₃ (math + physics): subadditive (same abstract evaluation)

  B + B (different receptors):
    → Touch (CT afferents) + Warmth (thermoreceptors)
    → DIFFERENT receptor types, DIFFERENT peripheral pathways
    → Minimal substrate overlap → little competition
    → Signal_total ≈ Signal_B1 + Signal_B2
    → = NEAR-ADDITIVE

    Observable: Được ôm (touch) trong chăn ấm (warmth)
    ≈ sum of touch alone + warmth alone.
    Both fire independently → no receptor competition.

    Exception: if same receptor activated (sustained touch + moving touch
    on same skin area) → competition → subadditive.


  ❷ CROSS-TYPE INTERACTION (A + B) = MODULATION:

  ⭐ This is NOT addition or multiplication.
  This is A GATE MODULATION — already drilled in R18 (insula gradient).

  B signal fires (posterior insula, ~20-100ms)
  → A evaluation fires parallel (~50-200ms)
  → Anterior insula INTEGRATES: A modulates B experience

  4 OUTCOMES (from §3.7 + §3.13, unified here):

  ┌──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ A Gate Setting    │ Compound Result                          │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A positive       │ SUPERADDITIVE: A amplifies B             │
  │ (trusted person) │ Compound > A_alone + B_alone             │
  │                  │ Mechanism: safety context OPENS gate →   │
  │                  │ B signal amplified by anterior insula    │
  │                  │ → qualitatively RICHER experience        │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A negative       │ SUBTRACTIVE: A suppresses/overrides B    │
  │ (stranger,       │ Compound = NEGATIVE despite B positive   │
  │  threat)         │ Mechanism: danger context CLOSES gate → │
  │                  │ B signal overridden by A evaluation     │
  │                  │ → net unpleasant                         │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A absent         │ RAW B: no modulation                     │
  │ (infant, PFC     │ Compound = B alone (unmodulated)         │
  │  offline)        │ = "Pure Type B experience"               │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A conflicted     │ NON-LINEAR: qualitatively NEW            │
  │ (attracted       │ Neither sum nor product — arousal +      │
  │  stranger)       │ caution = ambiguous compound             │
  │                  │ ACC signals conflict (🟢 Botvinick 2004) │
  └──────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┘

  → Cross-type interaction = MODULATION, not arithmetic.
  → A controls the GAIN of B, does not add to B.
  → Consistent with R18 insula gradient: insula = hardware for modulation.


  ❸ RELIEF (④) = SYSTEM-STATE MULTIPLIER:

  Relief = cortisol DROP = system-wide state change.
  QUALITATIVELY different from A or B signals:

    A/B = specific pathway signals (local, channel-specific)
    Relief = GLOBAL state change (cortisol affects entire brain)

  Cortisol drop → 3 simultaneous effects:
    ① Body muscles relax → sensory signals CLEARER
    ② PFC load decreases → perception RICHER
    ③ Opioid system disinhibited → opioid response STRONGER
      (🟢 chronic cortisol suppresses opioid sensitivity — stress analgesia literature)

  → Relief does NOT add reward. Relief MULTIPLIES reward
    by changing the SYSTEM STATE in which other signals are processed.
  → Compound_with_relief = base_compound × (1 + relief_factor)

  EVIDENCE:

    Eureka AFTER struggle >> Eureka WITHOUT struggle:
      Einstein: years struggle → E=mc² → "DAYS ecstasy"
      Student: 5 min problem → solve → "oh, cool" (seconds)
      SAME coherence reward type (A₃). VASTLY different magnitude.
      Difference = accumulated cortisol relief = multiplier.

    Comfort food AFTER stress >> same food relaxed:
      Same A₁ evaluation. But cortisol drop = multiplier.
      → "Comfort food" = food whose reward is MULTIPLIED by relief.

    Massage AFTER exercise >> massage without exercise:
      Same B signal (CT afferents). But muscle tension release
      = cortisol/NE drop = relief multiplier.

    🟢 Brickman & Campbell 1971: "contrast effect" —
    pleasure relative to prior state.
    Framework: cortisol relief = MECHANISM behind contrast effect.

  Relief factor = f(prior_pending_duration × cortisol_drop_magnitude):
    → Short pending (minutes): small relief → small multiplier (~1.2-1.5x)
    → Medium pending (days): moderate relief → moderate multiplier (~1.5-3x)
    → Long pending (years): large relief → large multiplier (~3-10x)
    → = WHY Einstein "DAYS" but student "seconds"
    → = WHY PhD completion euphoria > homework completion satisfaction


  ❹ TEMPORAL OVERLAP = COMPOUND QUALITY (R5↔R7 bridge):

  R5 finding: different reward types have different onset/peak/decay.
  R7 consequence: temporal OVERLAP determines HOW compound FEELS.

  3 TEMPORAL PATTERNS:

  SIMULTANEOUS PEAK (rare, maximum density):
    All channels peak at approximately same time.
    = MAXIMUM compound density → most intense experience.
    Example: orgasm = physical B + evaluation A + social + relief
    ALL peak together → one of strongest possible experiences.
    WHY rare: requires unusual temporal convergence.

  SEQUENTIAL PEAK (common, building experience):
    Channels peak one after another → experience "builds."
    Example: dinner with friends:
      B(touch): background constant
      A₀(taste): arrives first
      A₂(eval): builds with conversation
      Social: grows across evening
      Relief: slow fade of day's stress
    → Experience gets RICHER over time ("enjoyed more and more")
    → Each new layer shifts qualitative character.

  ASYNCHRONOUS (common, phased experience):
    Channels peak at very different times → distinct phases.
    Example: concert:
      Phase 1: visual (stage) → mild pleasant
      Phase 2: music → A₂ builds
      Phase 3: crowd energy → social + B (rhythm) → compound
      Phase 4: encore → relief ("thought it was over") → multiplier
      Phase 5: walking out → afterglow (consolidation)
    Each phase = qualitatively DIFFERENT experience.


  ❺ CONDITIONAL INTERACTION MODEL (unified):

  ⭐⭐ REPLACING BFM §4 simple additive model with CONDITIONAL model:

  NOT one interaction type — DEPENDS ON 4 variables:

  ┌─────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Variable            │ Effect on Interaction                     │
  ├─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ① Substrate overlap │ Same substrate (A+A): SUBADDITIVE        │
  │                     │ Different substrate (A+B, B+B): ADDITIVE │
  ├─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ② A gate direction  │ A positive: AMPLIFIES B → SUPERADDITIVE  │
  │                     │ A negative: SUPPRESSES B → SUBTRACTIVE   │
  │                     │ A absent: B RAW → no modulation          │
  │                     │ A conflicted: NON-LINEAR → ambiguous     │
  ├─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ③ Relief presence   │ With relief: MULTIPLICATIVE              │
  │                     │ Without relief: base interaction only     │
  ├─────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ④ Temporal overlap  │ Simultaneous: MAXIMUM compound           │
  │                     │ Sequential: BUILDING experience          │
  │                     │ Asynchronous: PHASED experience          │
  └─────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┘

  QUALITATIVE FORMULA (not mathematical precision):

    Compound = [Σ(same-substrate signals, subadditive)]
             + [A_gate × B_signals (modulation)]
             × [1 + relief_factor (multiplier)]
             × [temporal_overlap_coefficient]

  Where:
    A_gate ∈ {amplify(+), suppress(-), absent(0), conflicted(±)}
    relief_factor = f(pending_duration × cortisol_drop)
    temporal_overlap = f(synchrony of peak timings)

  ⚠️ This is QUALITATIVE model — not mathematical equation.
  Captures interaction TYPES and DIRECTIONS, not precise magnitudes.


  ❻ EDGE CASES RE-ANALYZED WITH CONDITIONAL MODEL:

  Sex (§3.7⑤ — compound NHẤT):
    ① A+B cross-type: A (attractiveness) + B (physical) = modulation
    ② A gate positive: → SUPERADDITIVE
    ③ Relief: tension release at orgasm = multiplier
    ④ Temporal: orgasm = SIMULTANEOUS peak → maximum
    → 4 variables ALL maximally favorable → strongest compound

  Stranger touch (§3.7②):
    ① A+B cross-type: A (evaluation) + B (CT afferents) = modulation
    ② A gate NEGATIVE: → SUBTRACTIVE
    ③ Relief: none (stress ADDED)
    ④ Temporal: immediate
    → A gate reversal → compound NEGATIVE despite positive B
    → Model explains why same stimulus = opposite experience

  Comfort food alone after stressful day:
    ① A+A within-type: food = opioid → subadditive ceiling
    ② No B component significant
    ③ Relief: stress drop = MULTIPLIER → elevates modest food reward
    ④ Temporal: sequential (eat → relief builds)
    → Relief multiplier = primary driver of "comfort" in comfort food
    → Same food without stress = ordinary (no multiplier)

  Concert with friends:
    ① A+A (music + social): some subadditive opioid overlap
    ② A+B (rhythm/movement): A gate positive → superadditive
    ③ Relief: end-of-week → mild multiplier
    ④ Temporal: SEQUENTIAL → experience builds
    → Multiple compound types LAYERED → very rich experience

  Bad massage (§3.7④):
    ① A+B cross-type: A (technique eval) + B (CT)
    ② A gate NEGATIVE ("wrong technique"): → SUBTRACTIVE
    ③ No relief (frustration ADDED)
    ④ Temporal: sustained → persistent negative compound
    → A negative OVERRIDES B positive → net unpleasant


  🔴 TESTABLE PREDICTIONS:

  P-R7a: Cross-type compound (A+B) > sum of A_alone + B_alone
    → Music + massage hedonic rating > music rating + massage rating
    → Within-type (A+A, food + music) ≈ or < sum
    → Protocol: controlled hedonic ratings, 3 conditions each
    → Expected: A+B superadditive, A+A subadditive

  P-R7b: Relief multiplier proportional to prior pending duration
    → Same insight, variable struggle:
      Short struggle → modest reward
      Long struggle → intense reward
    → Magnitude difference >> complexity difference
    → Testable: controlled problem-solving with varied delay before solution

  P-R7c: A gate reversal flips ENTIRE compound instantly
    → Friend → stranger MID-MASSAGE: compound flips + to -
    → B signal UNCHANGED (same CT). Only A evaluation changes.
    → Transition time = A re-evaluation time (~200-500ms, R18)
    → Testable: social context manipulation during touch paradigm

  P-R7d: Simultaneous-peak compound > sequential-peak of SAME components
    → Orgasm (simultaneous) > building intimacy (sequential)
    → In PEAK intensity (not total reward over time)
    → Testable: hedonic peak ratings under synchronized vs staggered delivery


  R5↔R7 BRIDGE — TEMPORAL AND COMPOUND INTERLOCK:

  ┌──────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ R5 Finding           │ R7 Consequence                          │
  ├──────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ B onset precedes A   │ First feel of compound = B layer.       │
  │                      │ A modulation arrives AFTER.             │
  ├──────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ A₃ afterglow longest │ Compound with A₃ has longest total     │
  │                      │ duration (4-curve afterglow).           │
  ├──────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Temporal stack model │ Stack width × R7 interaction type       │
  │                      │ = compound quality (richness metric).   │
  ├──────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Relief extends       │ Relief multiplier extends compound      │
  │ duration             │ duration AND intensity.                 │
  └──────────────────────┴────────────────────────────────────────┘


  CROSS-REFERENCES:
    → §2.2 Profile table → compound = norm (confirmed, now FORMALIZED)
    → §3.5 Type A/B → orthogonal substrates = foundation for conditional model
    → §3.7 6 edge cases → RE-ANALYZED with conditional model (all fit)
    → §3.7 A Gates B → = variable ② in model
    → §3.11 R20 hedonic treadmill → A subadditive within-type explains treadmill
    → §3.13 R18 insula gradient → = neural implementation of A gate modulation
    → §3.14 R5 temporal model → = variable ④ in model
    → BFM §4 compound mechanism → REFINED: additive → conditional
    → Body-Coupling.md → coupling + compound = deep entity binding
    → 🟢 Peciña & Berridge 2005 — hedonic hotspot finite capacity
    → 🟢 Brickman & Campbell 1971 — contrast effect (= relief multiplier)
    → 🟢 Botvinick et al. 2004 — ACC conflict during A-conflicted state
```

### §3.16 — System Reconsolidation: Individual vs System-Level (v0.8 new: R15 drill)

```
⭐⭐ R15 DRILL — SYSTEM RECONSOLIDATION CONCEPT:

  QUESTION (from §10):
  "Psychedelic → schema landscape temporarily malleable
  → Just many individual reconsolidation windows? Hay mechanism riêng?
  Griffiths 2006: 1 session → lasting change. Mechanism chính xác?"

  ANSWER: CẢ HAI — nhưng system-level là EMERGENT PROPERTY.
  Individual reconsolidation = per-chunk. System reconsolidation = when
  ENOUGH chunks simultaneously labile → RELATIONSHIP STRUCTURE modifiable.
  = Phase transition, not just "nhiều cái cùng lúc."


  ❶ INDIVIDUAL vs SYSTEM RECONSOLIDATION:

  INDIVIDUAL RECONSOLIDATION (🟢 Nader et al. 2000):
    → Mỗi khi retrieve 1 memory → labile state → can modify → reconsolidate
    → = Per-chunk mechanism: chunk A → labile → modify → reconsolidate
    → Constraint: TOP-DOWN PRIORS VẪN ACTIVE
    → Surrounding hierarchy PULLS modified chunk BACK → change limited
    → Analogy: rearrange 1 đồ vật — room unchanged

  PSYCHEDELIC SYSTEM RECONSOLIDATION:
    → REBUS (🟢 Carhart-Harris & Friston 2019): ALL priors relaxed
    → DMN DISINTEGRATED (🟢 Carhart-Harris 2012, Tagliazucchi 2016)
    → Many chunks labile SIMULTANEOUSLY
    → Top-down hierarchy temporarily FLAT
    → = RELATIONSHIP STRUCTURE between chunks becomes modifiable
    → = Not just individual mountains reshapable — TOPOLOGY can shift

  WHY this is EMERGENT (not just "many individual reconsolidations"):
    → Individual reconsolidation: modify 1 chunk → hierarchy pulls back → revert
    → System reconsolidation: hierarchy ITSELF flat → new configuration can
      STABILIZE as new default → structural change
    → = Phase transition: water → steam ≠ "many hot molecules"
      = qualitative state change when enough elements simultaneously labile

  ┌────────────────────────┬──────────────────┬──────────────────────┐
  │ Mechanism              │ Scope            │ Lasting Change?      │
  ├────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ Individual             │ 1 chunk          │ Limited (hierarchy   │
  │ reconsolidation        │ per retrieval    │ pulls back)          │
  │ (🟢 Nader 2000)        │                  │                      │
  ├────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ Competitive            │ Per-chunk        │ Moderate (competing  │
  │ re-linking             │ (build alongside)│ chunks, months-years)│
  │ (Cortisol §10.5)       │                  │                      │
  ├────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ System                 │ HIERARCHY-WIDE   │ HIGH (topology shift,│
  │ reconsolidation        │ (topology change)│ new default config)  │
  │ (psychedelic)          │                  │                      │
  ├────────────────────────┼──────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ Trauma compilation     │ HIERARCHY-WIDE   │ HIGH (but NEGATIVE   │
  │ (violent flip)         │ (but NEGATIVE)   │ direction)           │
  │ (Cortisol §10.1)       │                  │                      │
  └────────────────────────┴──────────────────┴──────────────────────┘


  ❷ 3-STEP MECHANISM: Destabilize → Reorganize → Consolidate:

  Step 1 — DESTABILIZE (session onset):
    → 5-HT2A agonism → DMN network disintegration
    → Top-down priors lose constraint power
    → Chunks labile, relationships between chunks modifiable
    → = "Ground becomes soft" — topology CAN shift

  Step 2 — REORGANIZE (during session, hours):
    → Body receives unprecedented combination of signals
    → BFM 3 dynamics SIMULTANEOUSLY + UNCOORDINATED:
      Chunk-Shift: valence re-evaluate EN MASSE (schemas lose constraint)
      Chunk-Miss: baseline patterns fire DIFFERENTLY → continuous miss signals
      Chunk-Gap: ACC detects EVERYWHERE (all patterns disrupted)
    → Under safe context: new chunk-to-chunk links compile
    → Guide/therapist provides framework for reorganization
    → Emotional peak during session → DEEP compilation (same as trauma mechanism)
    → = "Landscaping while the ground is soft"

  Step 3 — CONSOLIDATE (post-session, days-weeks):
    → Sleep: new configuration consolidates (🟢 Walker 2017)
    → Integration therapy: PFC processes new configuration
    → New hierarchy stabilizes → becomes NEW default
    → WITHOUT proper consolidation → revert OR chaotic patterns
    → = WHY integration sessions CRITICAL for lasting change


  ❸ MIRROR MECHANISM: System Reconsolidation ↔ Trauma Compilation:

  ⭐ KEY INSIGHT: These are the SAME mechanism, DIFFERENT direction.

    TRAUMA COMPILATION (Cortisol §10.1):
      → Single extreme event → emotional peak → deep compilation
      → Direction: AVOIDANCE (unsafe context → cortisol tag)
      → Result: lasting NEGATIVE structural change
      → = Hierarchy reorganized around threat

    SYSTEM RECONSOLIDATION (therapeutic):
      → Psychedelic session → emotional intensity → deep compilation
      → Direction: APPROACH (safe context → opioid tag)
      → Result: lasting POSITIVE structural change
      → = Hierarchy reorganized toward flexibility

    SAME POWER:
      → Both: single event → lasting structural change
      → Both: emotional peak → deep chunk compilation
      → Both: hierarchy-level reorganization

    DIFFERENT DIRECTION:
      → Set & setting = "ensuring compilation direction = APPROACH
        during hierarchy-flat window"
      → = WHY set & setting is not optional — it IS the mechanism


  ❹ 4 CONDITIONS FOR THERAPEUTIC SYSTEM RECONSOLIDATION:

  ┌────────────────────┬──────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────┐
  │ Condition          │ Met → IMPROVEMENT        │ Not met → RISK           │
  ├────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ ① Sufficient       │ Hierarchy flat enough    │ Too little: surface only │
  │   destabilization  │ for structural change    │ Too much: overwhelming   │
  │                    │                          │ → body defense shutdown  │
  ├────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ ② Safe context     │ Compilation direction    │ Unsafe: avoidance tag    │
  │   (set & setting)  │ = APPROACH → positive    │ → traumatic restructure  │
  │                    │ restructuring            │ = "bad trip" → lasting   │
  │                    │                          │ negative change          │
  ├────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ ③ Guided           │ Therapist provides       │ No guide: chaotic        │
  │   recompilation    │ framework → coherent     │ reorganization →         │
  │                    │ new pattern              │ unstable configuration   │
  ├────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ ④ Consolidation    │ Sleep + integration      │ No integration: new      │
  │   post-session     │ → new config stabilizes  │ patterns don't stabilize │
  │                    │ → lasting change         │ → revert or chaotic      │
  └────────────────────┴──────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────┘

  → GOLDILOCKS PRINCIPLE APPLIES (H10 P4):
    Too little destabilization → no structural change
    Too much → overwhelming → body defense
    Just right → structural change → lasting improvement
    = WHY dosing matters, WHY set & setting matters


  ❺ FRAMEWORK-SPECIFIC MECHANISM:

  Chunk dynamics during system reconsolidation:
    → Chunk-Shift: valence assignments FLUID (priors relaxed)
      → "Điều tôi ghét" có thể re-evaluate → neutral/positive
      → VP mechanism with hierarchy constraints REMOVED
    → Chunk-Miss: expected patterns DON'T fire
      → Continuous miss signals → intense body-feedback
      → BUT without threat context = NOVELTY direction → approach compile
    → Chunk-Gap: ACC fires continuously
      → "Everything is a gap" → new connections possible
      → Collins & Loftus 1975 spreading activation UNRESTRAINED

  Anchor-Schema implication:
    → Deep anchors (Anchor-Schema.md) normally RESIST change
    → During system reconsolidation: anchors temporarily LOOSENED
    → Can form NEW anchors at foundation level
    → Griffiths 2006 "mystical experience" = possibly NEW deep anchor formation
    → Post-session change = new anchor established during hierarchy-flat window

  Conditional Interaction Model (§3.15) implication:
    → During session: unprecedented signal combinations → compound
    → Cross-type (A+B) → SUPERADDITIVE
    → Relief (if chronic depression/anxiety → cortisol drop) → MULTIPLIER
    → = Explains "profound experience" reports


  🔴 TESTABLE PREDICTIONS:

  P-R15a: System reconsolidation effect ∝ degree of DMN disruption
    → More DMN disintegration → more hierarchy flattening → more change
    → Measurable: fMRI DMN connectivity change × lasting personality change
    → Expected: correlation between acute DMN disruption and long-term outcome

  P-R15b: Lasting change REQUIRES consolidation (sleep quality matters)
    → Poor sleep after session → less lasting change
    → Measurable: sleep quality (SWS+REM) post-session × outcome at 6 months
    → Expected: better sleep → better long-term outcome

  P-R15c: Set & setting → compilation direction → determines outcome valence
    → Same substance, same dose: safe → positive, unsafe → negative
    → Measurable: context quality × outcome direction (not just magnitude)
    → Expected: context STRONGER predictor than dose for outcome valence

  P-R15d: Repeated sessions show diminishing structural returns
    → First session: maximum structural change potential (hierarchy first flattened)
    → Later sessions: already restructured → less topology to shift
    → Measurable: magnitude of change per session across series
    → Expected: diminishing returns for STRUCTURAL change


  CROSS-REFERENCES:
    → §5b.4: REBUS + DMN disintegration (FOUNDATION)
    → R11 ✅: Psychedelic = schema destabilization (GAP this RESOLVES)
    → R16: Strategy A→B transition (BRIDGE — reconsolidation can address B default)
    → Cortisol §10: Trauma loop 4-stage (MIRROR mechanism)
    → Cortisol §7.6: Re-association 3-path (individual vs system-level)
    → BFM §3: 3 chunk dynamics (uncoordinated during reconsolidation)
    → VP: valence propagation with hierarchy constraints removed
    → Anchor-Schema.md: deep anchors temporarily loosened
    → §3.15 Conditional Interaction Model: compound signals during session
    → H10 P4: Goldilocks applies to destabilization degree
    → 🟢 Nader et al. 2000 — individual reconsolidation established
    → 🟢 Carhart-Harris & Friston 2019 — REBUS model
    → 🟢 Griffiths et al. 2006 — single session lasting change
    → 🟢 Walker 2017 — sleep-dependent consolidation
```

### §3.17 — Strategy A→B Transition: Defense Strategy Switch (v0.8 new: R16 drill)

```
⭐⭐ R16 DRILL — STRATEGY A→B TRANSITION MECHANISM:

  QUESTION (from §10):
  "Khi nào body chuyển từ fight/flight sang dissociation?
  Có threshold? Hardware variation? Lanius: dissociative subtype
  MORE in early childhood trauma"

  ANSWER: A→B transition = NOT intensity threshold.
  = ESCAPE POSSIBILITY ASSESSMENT × compiled A outcome history
  × developmental window. Caregiver trauma = triple impossibility.


  ❶ CLARIFICATION: A and B ARE ALTERNATIVE CONFIGURATIONS:

  Strategy A — Active (Fight/Flight):
    → NE flood → PFC mode ④ Disconnected → amygdala rules → escape
    → = 500M+ years. DEFAULT response. Most ancient.

  Strategy B — Passive (Freeze/Dissociate):
    → PFC mode ⑤ Hyperactivated → suppress amygdala → disconnect pain
    → = Khi A fails (inescapable). Newer mechanism.

  ⭐ CRITICAL INSIGHT: A→B ≠ intensity threshold.
    If only intensity: higher threat → A MORE intense (amygdala stronger)
    → Strategy A ESCALATES, not switches to B.
    A→B = ESCAPE POSSIBILITY ASSESSMENT — qualitatively different variable.

  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ High threat detected                                      │
  │     ↓                                                     │
  │ NE flood + cortisol spike                                 │
  │     ↓                                                     │
  │ ┌─── Escape possible? ───┐                               │
  │ │                         │                               │
  │ YES                      NO                               │
  │ ↓                        ↓                                │
  │ Strategy A               Strategy B                       │
  │ PFC ④ Disconnected       PFC ⑤ Hyperactivated            │
  │ Amygdala RULES           PFC SUPPRESSES amygdala          │
  │ Fight/Flight             Freeze/Dissociate                │
  │ ↓                        ↓                                │
  │ Escape → safe            Survive → pain disconnected      │
  │ Recovery: fast           Recovery: slow (damage)          │
  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  SAME neurochemical cocktail (high NE, high cortisol)
  → DIFFERENT PFC configuration selected by escape assessment
  → A and B = PARALLEL OPTIONS, not sequential stages


  ❷ 3 VARIABLES DETERMINING A→B TRANSITION:

  VARIABLE ① — ESCAPE POSSIBILITY ASSESSMENT (core):

    Body evaluates: "Can I fight or flee?"
    → CAN escape → Strategy A WORKS → stay in A
    → CANNOT escape → Strategy A FUTILE → switch to B

    Assessment mechanism (🟡):
      → Subcortical: amygdala + basal ganglia evaluate escape routes
      → Compiled chunks: past "fight → caught → worse" → A futile PRE-COMPILED
      → NOT conscious PFC decision → body-level assessment
      → Speed: ~100-500ms (faster than PFC deliberation)

    KEY: variable = "CAN I escape?" NOT "how strong is threat?"
      → Threat cực mạnh + escape possible = Strategy A (fight/flight)
      → Threat vừa + escape IMPOSSIBLE = Strategy B (dissociate)
      → = WHY child hit LIGHTLY but CHRONICALLY → dissociates
        (cannot escape parent, not because pain is extreme)
      → = WHY adult robbed at gunpoint (strong threat) → fight/flight
        (CAN potentially escape, run, resist)


  VARIABLE ② — COMPILED A OUTCOME HISTORY:

    Past A outcomes COMPILE into schema → affect FUTURE assessment:

    Past A successful (fought/fled → survived → safe):
      → Schema compiled: "A → works → safe"
      → Future threats: A fires DEFAULT, B rarely triggered
      → = Healthy defense. Most people.

    Past A failed ONCE (fought → punished, fled → caught):
      → Schema: "A → worse harm" (1 trial, emotional peak compile)
      → SIMILAR threats: A inhibited → B more likely
      → Generalization LIMITED — B only for similar contexts

    Past A failed REPEATEDLY (chronic abuse):
      → Schema compiled DEEPLY: "A → ALWAYS futile"
      → GENERALIZED A inhibition → B fires DEFAULT for ANY threat
      → = Childhood trauma pattern (🟢 Lanius 2010)
      → = Strategy B compiled as FOUNDATION, not just response


  VARIABLE ③ — AGE AT FIRST TRAUMA (developmental window):

    ⭐ Age determines WHETHER A IS EVEN POSSIBLE:

    INFANT/TODDLER (0-3 years):
      → Physically CANNOT fight adult caregiver
      → Physically CANNOT flee (dependent, immobile/slow)
      → A = IMPOSSIBLE by PHYSICS — not by assessment
      → B = ONLY OPTION from the start
      → B compiled as PRIMARY defense → FOUNDATION for all future
      → = Lanius: early childhood trauma → dissociative subtype

    CHILD (3-7 years):
      → Can fight weakly, can flee but caught
      → A ATTEMPTED but fails → A futile compiled
      → B develops as SECONDARY strategy
      → Both A and B schemas → context-dependent switching

    ADOLESCENT/ADULT:
      → A POSSIBLE (physical capacity present)
      → First trauma → A attempted → may succeed or fail
      → A failure → B compiled secondarily (backup, not foundation)
      → = Lanius: later trauma → re-experiencing subtype (A patterns)

    DEVELOPMENTAL MECHANISM:

    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │ Early childhood (0-3):                                      │
    │   A = physically impossible → B = ONLY option = FOUNDATION │
    │   All future defense schemas BUILD ON B foundation          │
    │   Even safe adult context → B fires first (deepest compile)│
    │                                                             │
    │ Later childhood/adult first trauma:                         │
    │   A = attempted → may fail → B = SECONDARY backup          │
    │   A schemas = FOUNDATION → B = escalation option            │
    │   Under overwhelming threat → A fails → B escalation       │
    └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘


  ❸ ATTACHMENT PARADOX — WHY CAREGIVER TRAUMA = MAXIMUM DISSOCIATION:

  ⭐ TRIPLE IMPOSSIBILITY MECHANISM:

  Normal threat: threat source ≠ attachment source
    → Strategy A: fight/flee FROM threat → TOWARD attachment figure
    → Attachment figure = safe base → cortisol drops → recovery
    → = Designed pathway. Works for ALL external threats.

  Caregiver threat: threat source = attachment source
    → CANNOT flee toward attachment figure (they ARE the threat)
    → CANNOT fight attachment figure (would lose ONLY safe base)
    → CANNOT flee FROM attachment figure (would lose survival resource)
    → = TRIPLE IMPOSSIBILITY:
      ❶ A impossible (can't fight/flee from survival source)
      ❷ B = only option (disconnect pain while MAINTAINING behavior)
      ❸ BUT: B must be PARTIAL (must still seek attachment = survival)

  Body's "impossible solution":
    → Dissociate pain → maintain approaching behavior → survive
    → = "Hug the person hurting you while not feeling the pain"
    → = Functional but COSTLY: emotional processing SHUT DOWN

  What compiles:
    → "relationship = pain disconnected from awareness"
    → Adult pattern: maintain relationships but CANNOT feel them fully
    → = Body-Coupling.md: "entanglement" with negative coupling

  🟢 Disorganized attachment (Main & Hesse 1990):
    → Infant shows contradictory behavior: approach + freeze + look away
    → = Body expressing BOTH "seek attachment" AND "dissociate threat"
    → = Observable evidence of triple impossibility mechanism


  ❹ HARDWARE VARIATION — WHO DEFAULTS TO B:

  4 HARDWARE FACTORS affecting A/B tendency:

  ┌─────────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Factor                  │ Effect on A/B tendency                 │
  ├─────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ① HPA axis sensitivity  │ More reactive → overwhelmed sooner    │
  │   (genetic)             │ → B threshold LOWER                   │
  │                         │ 🟢 HPA genetic variation (Yehuda 2016)│
  ├─────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ② PFC-amygdala          │ Stronger inhibitory pathway → easier  │
  │   connectivity          │ to suppress amygdala → B more access. │
  │                         │ 🟡 Consistent with connectivity lit.  │
  ├─────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ③ Vagal tone            │ High vagal → FREEZE accessible        │
  │                         │ (intermediate: parasympathetic        │
  │                         │ override of sympathetic)              │
  │                         │ 🟢🟡 Porges polyvagal (core verified) │
  ├─────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ ④ Epigenetic            │ Parental trauma → offspring HPA       │
  │   calibration           │ pre-calibrated → B threshold lower    │
  │                         │ 🟢 Yehuda 2016 transgenerational      │
  └─────────────────────────┴────────────────────────────────────────┘

  → Individual "weakness" is ACTUALLY calibration = f(4-tier: evolution ×
    development × culture × epigenetic)
  → NOT pathology but APPROPRIATE calibration for ancestors' environment
  → Mismatch when offspring environment actually safe → B fires unnecessarily


  ❺ B→A REVERSION: POSSIBLE BUT NEVER COMPLETE

  B→A transition possible when:

    ① Safe environment (no real threat):
      → Body learns "A is possible" (new context, no punishment)
      → Competitive re-linking (Cortisol §10.5)
      → New "A → safe outcome" chunks compile alongside "A → futile"
      → Timeline: months-years

    ② Somatic therapy specifically:
      → Body RE-LEARNS physical capacity: "I CAN push, I CAN run"
      → Deliberately activate A pathway in SAFE context
      → Type B reward (touch, body movement) as "backdoor" (§5b.3)
      → 🟢 Van der Kolk 2014: body-oriented therapy for trauma

    ③ Gradual exposure:
      → Small threats where A SUCCEEDS → compile "A works"
      → Goldilocks: threat small enough that A handles it
      → Progressive: gradually larger threats with A success
      → = Exposure therapy mechanism in framework terms

  CONSTRAINTS:
    → Complete reversal UNLIKELY for early childhood B foundation:
      B compiled FIRST → deepest chunks → persists underneath
    → FUNCTIONAL reversal: A becomes ACCESSIBLE, B remains as backup
      = "I CAN fight now, but under extreme stress I still dissociate"
    → = Not "cure" but expanded repertoire (A+B available, not just B)
    → = Cortisol §9.7: childhood trauma baseline NEVER = pre-trauma


  ❻ R15↔R16 BRIDGE — SYSTEM RECONSOLIDATION × B DEFAULT:

  ⭐ R15 ADDRESSES R16:

  Problem: Childhood B default = compiled DEEP → resistant to normal re-association
  Normal therapy: competitive re-linking → builds A alongside B → months-years, partial
  System reconsolidation: hierarchy FLAT → B FOUNDATION itself accessible

  Mechanism:
    → During system reconsolidation: B foundation temporarily LABILE
    → Under safe context: A pathways can compile AT FOUNDATION LEVEL
    → = Not building A on top of B — modifying B foundation itself
    → = WHY psychedelic-assisted therapy shows promise for treatment-resistant PTSD

  CAUTION:
    → B foundation = SURVIVAL strategy → removing without replacement = DANGEROUS
    → MUST provide safe context + guided A recompilation DURING destabilization
    → R15 condition ② (safe context) = ESPECIALLY critical for trauma
    → System reconsolidation without safety → re-traumatization risk HIGH


  🔴 TESTABLE PREDICTIONS:

  P-R16a: A→B transition correlates with ESCAPE POSSIBILITY, not threat INTENSITY
    → Inescapable moderate threat → more dissociation than escapable severe threat
    → Expected: escape possibility = stronger predictor than intensity
    → 🟢 Partially supported: Lanius 2010 inescapable childhood → dissociative

  P-R16b: Childhood trauma (< 3 years) → higher dissociative response ratio
    → Measurable: age at first trauma × dissociative symptom prevalence
    → Expected: earlier trauma → stronger B default
    → 🟢 Partially supported: Lanius 2010, Van der Kolk research

  P-R16c: Somatic therapy → reduces dissociative default (B→A expansion)
    → Measurable: dissociative symptom reduction after body-oriented therapy
    → Expected: somatic MORE effective than purely cognitive CBT for dissociative subtype
    → 🟢 Van der Kolk 2014: body-oriented therapy effective for trauma

  P-R16d: Caregiver-source trauma → MORE dissociation than non-caregiver
    at same intensity
    → Compare dissociative symptoms by source (parent vs stranger)
    → Expected: caregiver → triple impossibility → more dissociation
    → 🟡 Framework prediction — consistent with attachment literature


  CROSS-REFERENCES:
    → §5b.3: Dissociation = Mode 6 weaponized (FOUNDATION)
    → R12 ✅: Dissociation drilled (this section EXTENDS)
    → §3.16 R15: System reconsolidation (BRIDGE — addresses B default)
    → Threat.md §2: 5 intensity levels, PFC disconnect
    → Threat.md §3: Physical/Social/Anticipation × A/B strategies
    → Threat.md §4: Imposed threat (caregiver = imposed + attachment)
    → Cortisol §10: Trauma loop 4-stage (A→B = Stage 1 alternative pathway)
    → Cortisol §7.5: 4 threat thresholds
    → Cortisol §7.6: Re-association 3-path (B→A reversion)
    → Body-Base §7: Circuit breaker 3 pathways
    → Body-Coupling.md: entanglement with negative coupling (caregiver paradox)
    → §3.8 Development Gradient: B reward dominant in infancy (PARALLEL: B defense)
    → Type B reward "backdoor" for therapy (§5b.3, R9 resolved)
    → 🟢 Lanius et al. 2010 — 2 trauma subtypes
    → 🟢 Main & Hesse 1990 — disorganized attachment
    → 🟢 Van der Kolk 2014 — body-oriented therapy
    → 🟢 Yehuda 2016 — transgenerational cortisol
    → 🟡 Porges Polyvagal Theory — vagal brake hierarchy
```

### §3.18 — PFC Sub-Region × Function × Mode Mapping (v0.9 new: R2 drill)

```
⭐⭐ R2 DRILL — PFC SUB-REGION × FUNCTION MAPPING:

  QUESTION (from §10):
  "Map 24 PFC functions vào BOTH taxonomies (participation × configuration).
  DLPFC vs medial PFC vs OFC → serve functions nào cụ thể?"

  ANSWER: Mapping là 3D (MANY-TO-MANY), không phải 2D hay 1:1.
  24 functions × 6 sub-regions × 2 taxonomies.
  Key insight: dlPFC serves 15/24 functions → hub bottleneck.
  Configuration determines WHICH functions survive, not how many.


  ❶ 24 FUNCTIONS → 6 SUB-REGIONS (many-to-many):

  ⭐ Each function = PRIMARY sub-region + SECONDARY support.
  Each sub-region serves MULTIPLE functions. KHÔNG phải 1:1.

  OBSERVE (4):
  ┌────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────┬───────────────────┐
  │ Function               │ Primary    │ Secondary    │ Evidence          │
  ├────────────────────────┼────────────┼──────────────┼───────────────────┤
  │ ① Observe Feeling      │ vmPFC      │ ant. insula  │ 🟢 Damasio 1994   │
  │ ② Observe Body Vote    │ ACC        │ OFC          │ 🟢 Botvinick 2004 │
  │ ③ Observe Chunk Active │ dlPFC      │ mPFC         │ 🟡                │
  │ ④ Meta-cognition       │ mPFC       │ ACC          │ 🟢 Fleming 2012   │
  └────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────┴───────────────────┘

  HOLD (4):
  ┌────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────┬───────────────────┐
  │ ⑤ Hold ~4±1            │ dlPFC      │ —            │ 🟢 Goldman-R 1995 │
  │ ⑥ Quick Search         │ dlPFC      │ —            │ 🟢 Fuster 1973    │
  │ ⑦ Loose Hold           │ dlPFC ↓    │ mPFC/DMN ↑   │ 🟡 DMN creativity │
  │ ⑧ Active Lock          │ dlPFC      │ ACC (unresol)│ 🟢 Zeigarnik      │
  └────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────┴───────────────────┘

  PROCESS (6):
  ┌────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────┬───────────────────┐
  │ ⑨ Type 4 Linking       │ dlPFC      │ ACC          │ 🟡                │
  │ ⑩ Imagination          │ dlPFC+mPFC │ OFC          │ 🟢 Hassabis 2007  │
  │ ⑪ Domain-Check         │ dlPFC+ACC  │ OFC          │ 🟡                │
  │ ⑫ Label Creation       │ dlPFC+vlPFC│ Broca's      │ 🟡                │
  │ ⑬ Create New Chunks    │ dlPFC      │ ACC          │ 🟡                │
  │ ⑭ Modify Existing      │ dlPFC      │ vmPFC        │ 🟢 Nader 2000     │
  └────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────┴───────────────────┘

  ORCHESTRATE (6):
  ┌────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────┬───────────────────┐
  │ ⑮ Gate Attention TRN   │ dlPFC→TRN  │ —            │ 🟢 McAlonan 2008  │
  │ ⑯ Bias Spread. Activ.  │ dlPFC      │ cortical     │ 🟡                │
  │ ⑰ Invoke SPM           │ mPFC+vmPFC │ TPJ          │ 🟢 Saxe 2006      │
  │ ⑱ Inhibit Compiled     │ vlPFC      │ —            │ 🟢 Aron 2004      │
  │ ⑲ Override Satisf.     │ vlPFC+dlPFC│ ACC          │ 🟡                │
  │ ⑳ Change Environment   │ dlPFC      │ vmPFC+OFC    │ 🟡                │
  └────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────┴───────────────────┘

  STRATEGIC (4):
  ┌────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────┬───────────────────┐
  │ ㉑ Smooth Melody        │ ACC+dlPFC  │ vmPFC        │ 🟡                │
  │ ㉒ Choose Between Goals │ OFC+dlPFC  │ vmPFC        │ 🟢 Padoa-S 2011   │
  │ ㉓ Accept Temp. Disson. │ ACC+dlPFC  │ vmPFC        │ 🟡                │
  │ ㉔ Hijack Body-Input    │ dlPFC      │ motor cortex │ 🟡                │
  └────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────┴───────────────────┘


  ❷ KEY INSIGHT — dlPFC AS HUB + BOTTLENECK:

  Sub-region involvement count (primary + secondary):
    dlPFC:  15/24 — HUB. Working memory + cognitive control.
    ACC:     8/24 — QUALITY CONTROLLER. Conflict/error across all processes.
    vmPFC:   6/24 — EMOTIONAL BRIDGE. Body-signal integration.
    OFC:     5/24 — VALUE COMPUTER. Reward/value evaluation.
    mPFC:    5/24 — SELF + SOCIAL. Self-reference + social modeling.
    vlPFC:   3/24 — INHIBITION SPECIALIST. Stop-signal + rule.

  IMPLICATIONS:
    → dlPFC 15/24 = WM ~4±1 EXPLAINED: shared resource across TOO MANY functions
    → Flow requires dlPFC REALLOCATION: 15 competing → task-serving ONLY
    → Cortisol damages dlPFC dendrites (🟢 McEwen 2007) → 15/24 impaired
    → = WHY chronic stress "impairs everything PFC" — dlPFC is bottleneck
    → vlPFC only 3/24 BUT high-impact: damage = disinhibition (Phineas Gage)

  ⭐ WITHIN-REGION FUNCTION SPLITTING:
    dlPFC serves BOTH task-functions AND self-monitoring functions.
    In flow (config ②): task-functions ON, self-monitoring OFF.
    = Limb & Braun 2008: dlPFC "deactivation" = PARTIAL, not uniform.
    → SELECTIVE within single sub-region: task ON, self OFF.
    → = WHY flow feels "effortless" (self-monitoring off) but IS effective
      (task on, domain-check continuous).


  ❸ CONFIGURATION × FUNCTION SURVIVAL MATRIX:

  ⭐⭐ Which functions SURVIVE in which PFC configuration?

  Legend: ✅=active ⚠️=altered ❌=offline ⭐=enhanced

  ┌──────────────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┐
  │ Function         │①Normal │②Reallo │③Reconf │④Discon │⑤Hyper  │⑥Disint │
  ├──────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤
  │ ① Observe Feel   │ ✅     │ ⚠️task │ ⚠️alt  │ ❌     │ ⚠️over │ ❌flood│
  │ ② Body Vote      │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️sugg │ ❌     │ ❌supp │ ❌     │
  │ ③ Chunk Active   │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️     │ ❌     │ ⚠️narr │ ❌chao │
  │ ④ Meta-cognition │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ✅trn  │ ❌     │ ⚠️exc  │ ❌     │
  ├──────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤
  │ ⑤ Hold ~4±1      │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️     │ ❌     │ ⚠️rig  │ ❌     │
  │ ⑥ Quick Search   │ ✅     │ ✅fast │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ✅     │ ❌     │
  │ ⑦ Loose Hold     │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │
  │ ⑧ Active Lock    │ ✅     │ ❌flow │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ⚠️chr  │ ❌     │
  ├──────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤
  │ ⑨ Type 4 Link    │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️     │ ❌     │ ⚠️narr │ ❌     │
  │ ⑩ Imagination    │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️sugg │ ❌     │ ⚠️dist │ ❌     │
  │ ⑪ Domain-Check   │ ✅     │ ✅cont │ ⚠️     │ ❌     │ ⚠️bias │ ❌     │
  │ ⑫ Label          │ ✅     │ ✅     │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ✅     │ ❌     │
  │ ⑬ Create Chunks  │ ✅     │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │
  │ ⑭ Modify Chunks  │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ⭐wind │
  ├──────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤
  │ ⑮ Gate Attention │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️redir│ ❌     │ ⚠️narr │ ❌     │
  │ ⑯ Bias Activ.    │ ✅     │ ✅strg │ ⚠️redir│ ❌     │ ⚠️rig  │ ❌     │
  │ ⑰ Invoke SPM     │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │
  │ ⑱ Inhibit        │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ⭐MAX  │ ❌     │
  │ ⑲ Override Sat.  │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ⚠️chr  │ ❌     │
  │ ⑳ Change Environ │ ✅     │ ❌foc  │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌froz │ ❌     │
  ├──────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤
  │ ㉑ Smooth Melody  │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ⚠️     │ ❌     │ ❌rig  │ ❌     │
  │ ㉒ Choose Goals   │ ✅     │ ❌one  │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌stck │ ❌     │
  │ ㉓ Accept Disson. │ ✅     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │
  │ ㉔ Hijack Body-In │ ✅     │ ✅task │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │ ❌     │
  └──────────────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┘

  CONFIGURATION PROFILES (approximate active/altered/enhanced):
    ①Normal:     24/0/0  — all functions available
    ②Realloc:    ~14/0/0 — task-serving subset (flow)
    ③Reconfig:   ~10/4/0 — suggestion-guided (hypnosis, meditation)
    ④Disconn:    0/0/0   — all PFC offline (acute threat)
    ⑤HyperAct:   ~3/8/1  — inhibit⭐ + meta-excessive + rigid (dissociation)
    ⑥Disinteg:   0/0/1   — only ⑭ Modify Chunks ENHANCED (reconsolidation)


  ❹ CRITICAL FINDING — CONFIG ⑥ × FUNCTION ⑭:

  Config ⑥ (psychedelic disintegration):
  → Nearly ALL functions offline → no quality control
  → BUT ⑭ Modify Existing Chunks = ENHANCED
  → = System reconsolidation (R15) MECHANISM EXPLAINED:
    Config ⑥ opens modification window WHILE disabling normal PFC control
  → = BOTH the opportunity (chunks modifiable) AND the risk (no QC)
  → = WHY guided therapy REQUIRED: guide provides external QC
    when internal QC (PFC functions ⑪⑬⑱) all offline
  → Connects to R15 condition ③: guided recompilation
  → = "Ground soft (hierarchy flat) + no gardener (PFC off)
    = therapist must BE the gardener"


  ❺ CRITICAL FINDING — CONFIG ⑤ DISSOCIATION PROFILE:

  Config ⑤ (dissociative hyperactivation) = 4 FUNCTIONS WEAPONIZED:
  → ⑱ Inhibit = ⭐MAXIMUM → emotional numbness (amygdala suppressed)
  → ④ Meta-cognition = ⚠️EXCESSIVE → "watching self from outside"
    = depersonalization (🟢 Sierra & Berrios 1998)
  → ⑧ Active Lock = ⚠️CHRONIC → hypervigilance (cannot release)
  → ⑲ Override = ⚠️CHRONIC → "going through motions" without feeling
  → = 4 functions designed for SHORT-TERM use → CHRONIC = damage
  → Connects to R16: Strategy B = Config ⑤ = 4 functions weaponized
  → Connects to §5b.3: Drive Mode 6 weaponized = ⑱+⑲ specifically


  ❻ PARTICIPATION × CONFIGURATION: ORTHOGONAL BUT CONSTRAINED:

  NOT all combinations possible:

  ┌──────────────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┬────────┐
  │ Participation    │①Normal │②Reallo │③Reconf │④Discon │⑤Hyper  │⑥Disint │
  ├──────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤
  │ Mode 1 Absent    │ —      │ —      │ —      │ ✅     │ —      │ —      │
  │ Mode 2 Monitor   │ ✅     │ —      │ ⚠️rare │ —      │ —      │ —      │
  │ Mode 3 Spinning  │ ✅     │ —      │ —      │ —      │ ⚠️chr  │ —      │
  │ Mode 4 Resolve   │ ✅     │ ✅flow │ ✅trn  │ —      │ —      │ —      │
  │ Mode 5 Strategic │ ✅     │ —      │ ✅trn  │ —      │ —      │ —      │
  │ Mode 6 Override  │ ✅     │ —      │ —      │ —      │ ✅diss │ —      │
  └──────────────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┘

  NATURAL PAIRINGS:
    Mode 1 + Config ④ = Acute threat (PFC absent BECAUSE disconnected)
    Mode 3 + Config ⑤ = Anxious dissociation (spinning + hyperactivated)
    Mode 4 + Config ② = Flow state (resolve + reallocated to task)
    Mode 6 + Config ⑤ = Clinical dissociation (override + hyperactivated)
    Config ⑥ = OUTSIDE participation spectrum (all modes break down)

  IMPOSSIBLE COMBINATIONS:
    Mode 1 + Config ⑤ = can't hyperactivate AND be absent
    Mode 4 + Config ④ = can't resolve with PFC disconnected
    Mode 5 + Config ⑥ = can't be strategic when hierarchy disintegrated
    → Constraints FOLLOW from sub-region requirements


  ❼ BRIDGE INSIGHTS (R2 ↔ previous drill findings):

  R2 ↔ R15 (System Reconsolidation):
    Config ⑥ × function ⑭ = MECHANISM for hierarchy-flat → modification window.
    Guide = external replacement for ⑪ Domain-Check (offline in config ⑥).

  R2 ↔ R16 (Strategy A→B):
    Strategy A = Config ④ (PFC disconnected, subcortical takes over).
    Strategy B = Config ⑤ (PFC hyperactivated, 4 functions weaponized).
    A and B = DIFFERENT configurations, not different intensities.

  R2 ↔ R5 (Temporal Stack):
    Onset differences = partly f(which sub-regions involved).
    B (~20ms): posterior insula only, no PFC involvement.
    A₃ (~1-5s): dlPFC + ACC + OFC = multiple sub-regions sequentially.

  R2 ↔ R7 (Compound Interaction):
    A Gate B = OFC/vmPFC evaluation → anterior insula integration.
    = Sub-region PIPELINE, not single locus.
    Compound quality = f(how many sub-regions SIMULTANEOUSLY active).

  R2 ↔ R12 (Dissociation):
    §5b.3 "Mode 6 weaponized" NOW grounded:
    Mode 6 = ⑱ Inhibit + ⑲ Override → 2 specific functions.
    Config ⑤ ADDS: ④ Meta-cognition excessive + ⑧ Active Lock chronic.
    = 4 functions total → dissociation PROFILE at function level.


  🔴 TESTABLE PREDICTIONS:

  P-R2a: Flow (config ②) should show dlPFC SPLIT — task-serving active,
    self-monitoring inactive — NOT uniform dlPFC change.
    → Testable: high-resolution fMRI during flow with sub-region analysis
    → Expected: dissociation WITHIN dlPFC, not uniform deactivation

  P-R2b: Dissociation (config ⑤) should show vlPFC + ACC hyperactivated
    while most other sub-regions reduced or rigid.
    → Testable: sub-region analysis dissociative vs re-experiencing PTSD
    → Expected: vlPFC↑ + ACC↑ + amygdala↓ (not uniform PFC↑)

  P-R2c: Psychedelic (config ⑥) should show ⑭ Modify Chunks ENHANCED
    while ⑤ Hold + ⑱ Inhibit + ⑪ Domain-Check impaired.
    → Testable: reconsolidation + WM + inhibition tasks during psilocybin
    → Expected: memory modification ↑, WM capacity ↓, inhibition ↓

  P-R2d: dlPFC overload should predict WM failure at LOWER loads when
    multiple competing functions demanded simultaneously.
    → Testable: dual-task paradigm (WM + inhibition + social modeling)
    → Expected: WM capacity drops with competing dlPFC demands


  CROSS-REFERENCES:
